From: "Robert G. Brown" <rgb@phy.duke.edu>
> 
> Are you using PVM today?

Yes and no.  I'm not using it "today", but I'm using it as part of the
project I'm working on (just not that part I'm CURRENTLY working on).

> What are your application(s)?

Dynamical numericalj simulation of d-lattice-dimension O(n) Heisenberg
Models.

> How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

A farm of up to 32 Sparcstations of varying vintage (single SS-I
desktop CPUs through 4x Ross HyperSparc CPUs in SS-10's and 630's).  I
made some effort to run on heterogeneous machines, but it was too
difficult to keep code consistent across platforms that lacked an ANSI
C compiler or had different systems libraries.  Right now I'm working
primarily on a farm of Sparc CPU's that gives me around 250 MFLOPS
sustained on coarsely parallelized von Neummann code running in
master/slave mode, WHILE other folks are using the consoles of many of
those machines for standard Unix activities.  The farm is scalable,
and I hope to get it up to .5-1 GFLOPS over the next year as we
upgrade desktop computing facilities in our department and install
additional compute servers.

> Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.

Hmmm, it has been nine months or more since I last worked with it, but
as I recall there are several features that I would like to see
implemented or improved.

1) The processor monitor/control facility is (to say the least)
primitive.  It should return as much information as ps -auxww (BSD)
does on the machine in question for each running process under
control.  It should also allow any (Unix) signal to be sent to those
processes -- I found it necessary to be able to send STOP,CONT, USR1
and USR2 to some of my processes -- INTR and KILL are other natural
candidates for "rogue" processes.  Yes, I could (and did) rsh a ps and
rsh a kill, but this involved a complicated combination of using the
monitor to identify a troubled process, figuring out the machine it
was on, figuring out its (Unix) PID and (Unix) status, and sending it
a (Unix) signal, all the while popping in and out of the monitor or
using multiple windows.  Although not strictly necessary, it would be
wonderful to have a nifty X-client for the monitor program with
buttons and data entry lines and not just a command line version.

2) One of the HARDEST problems to solve in contemporary network
programming is how to write an numerical application with a
non-trivial execution loop (that might run for minutes to hours in a
single loop pass or days or weeks in total) and still allow real-time
program interruption for modification of its run state.  This problem
is especially irritating when one is trying to write a program with an
X-based front end/graphical display.  Current solutions include:
  a) Just use blocking or non-blocking I/O somewhere inside the main
event loop (X or otherwise).  This is fine if the execution loop is
grained to complete in <.1 sec, terrible if it completes in >10 sec
(so one has to wait, and wait, and wait, for the program to get to the
I/O statement).  Note that I disallow entirely the option of polling
in the innermost loops for both efficiency and blocking reasons.
  b) Separate the front end and the main loop into different programs,
called or forked or rsh'd as appropriate.  Set up a the I/O inside the
short event loop of the control program.  Set up sockets and/or pipes
and a signal mechanism to asynchronously interrupt the execution
module, set a flag to interrupt the innermost loops at a suitable
point (a simple conditional is much cheaper than polling for I/O),
handle some I/O in a controlled manner, and resume execution, or
restart the program, or terminate it after writing out its current
state, or whatever.

Note that I have figured out how to do all or most of this with
standard calls and tools -- but doing it is extremely non-trivial
network programming, especially when master (front end) and slave are
on different CPU's.  You could Make The World A Better Place if you
could construct a simple library of function calls that would reduce
all the hard part of this (fork/exec/rsh'ing, building the socket I/O
channels, establishing the signal mechanism that tells the slave to
listen to the master via the channel, and finally making the messaging
channel reliable) to boilerplate.  Quite a bit of this is already in
pvm (one reason I like it) but there's quite a bit missing, especially
on the asynchronous interrupt and signal support side (see item 1, for
example).

As a test case and demonstration, you should build a simple
demonstration of an X front end that serves as a mandelbrot DISPLAY
(only) with buttons and sliders and all, and a pvm-driven set of
clients that run asynchronously and can be interrupted and reset at
any time from the front end.  X-based mandelbrot programs abound, but
the all suffer from the annoying feature that they are not
interruptible in the main X event loop until they finish their current
picture, unless they poll for I/O in the "wrong place".  This can take
a LONG time, or waste a LOT OF time, depending on which you choose to
do.

If you build the support routines needed to do this as a standard part
of pvm and make them really easy to use and functional, you could even
submit the result to the X-Consortium as a contributed library to be
included with the standard release, as it would meet a real need and
fix a real shortcoming of X.  I know many physicists who have
struggled with this particular problem and (usually) worked out their
own solution at the cost of reinventing dozens of network programming
wheels or (occassionally) just thrown up their hands in disgust and
run/interrupted/reset things more simply, more expensively, and less
conveniently by hand.

3) Finally, yes, an interactive parallel (x-based) debugger would
surely help debug the really hard problems that can arise in parallel
code.  When last I used your program, I don't think that it had one,
although a friend did mention that you have started to provide some
sort of facility in this regard.  Keep it up.  Eventually one would
like to be able to single step and debug code running on multiple
processors from a single point of development inside some sort of
sensibly designed GUI.

> ps. Previous survey results are available through World Wide Web at
>     http://www.epm.ornl.gov/pvm/

Thanks, I'll check it out.

   rgb

Robert G. Brown	                       http://www.phy.duke.edu/~rgb
Duke University Dept. of Physics
Box 90305
Durham, N.C. 27708-0305
Phone: 1-919-660-2567  Fax: 919-660-2525     email:rgb@phy.duke.edu

From: <rfedors@VIS.ColoState.EDU>

We are currently using pvm in two different Monte Carlo problems.  One is a
radiation heat problem which has random emittance of "photons".  The second
is running random realizations of groundwater flow problems.  

> How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
 
Short answer is 8 SGIs (Irix5.2 & 4.05) and 3 SUNs (SunOS 4.1.1.2) all of
which are single processor machines.

The long answer:
Although we are a visualization lab (data modeling, geometric modeling, video
production, etc), two of the staffers are engineers whose primary research
focus requires extensive numerical work.  We both thought that pvm might 
be an additional tool for our work.  We have pvm running on 3 SUNs and
8 Silicon Graphics machines.  All of our machines are connected by ether net
although we are considering ATM or FDDI.  We are not doing any shared memory
pvm programming and do not envision future work in that area.  This is because
our primary goals are to solve engineering problems, not to make advances in
high performance computing.  Thus simple calls to start discrete sub-problems
on other machines, as the machines become available, is exactly what we
want out of pvm.  People like us rely upon examples in the pvm documentation
to quickly get things going.  We do not want to take the time to learn the 
verbiage of computer experts, and thus we appreciated the examples in the
documentation and encourage more examples illustrating the capabilities
and tricks of pvm. 


Randy Fedors    rfedors@vis.colostate.edu
  Civil Engineering Dept < Ph.D. student Groundwater Program > (303)491-8202  
  Computer Visualization Lab < Visualization Consultant  > (303)491-1578
Colorado State University, Fort Collins, Colorado 80523

From: <Vincent.Rijmen@esat.kuleuven.ac.be>

I am using PVM today, on a cluster of workstations (DEC stations with ULTRIX,
HP stations with HP-UX, SUNs with SUNOS) and a pentium with Linux.
In total there are more than 80 stations, but most of the time I only
use 10 or 20 of them. 

My applications are cryptanalytic attacks. Some of the most successfull
attacks on for instance the DES use lots of identical operations, easy
to distribute over lots of processors.

The problem I have is that sometimes I lose a machine from the cluster,
and that not all the hosts are aware of this: if I start with 50 hosts,
after a night I typically lose 1 or 2 hosts (that is due to network
problems here), but some of the other 48 hosts think they are still
with 50. The 2 lost hosts sometimes think they are still in the group.

Perhaps that could be improved ?

Vincent

From: "Robert G. Brown" <rgb@phy.duke.edu>

> Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.

Addendum to previous note:

  a) Distribute the software directly through the Web page you
advertised.  Why force potential users to go through netlib?
  b) Your web server seems sluggish.  Move the primary pvm
distribution off onto an SS20 or something, mirror it on the (possibly
overloaded) netlib server, and make it available via
anon-ftp/gopher/WWW as WELL as netlib.  Frankly, netlib is an idea
whose time has completely and irrevocably passed with the overwhelming
acceptance and universality of WWW/Mosaic.  The whole netlib
distribution should now be made available ONLY through the WWW.  Feel
free to pass this idea on to its keepers (they probably know it
already).
  c) Looking through the release notes through 3.3.6, it looks like
several of the features I suggest are still absent.  I suggest that
you really look carefully into the signal/non-blocking I/O problem and
work out a better solution than currently seems implemented, and
better control and debugging features are always welcome...

    rgb

From: "Alex Matro" <matro@haydn.chm.uri.edu>

Q1: Are you using PVM today?
A1: Yes.

Q2: What are your application(s)?
A2: We are using Monte Carlo simulations to calculate thermodynamic
properties of systems where we need to know the Boltzmann distribution
at higher temperatures to ensure proper sampling of the configuration space.
[See "Reducing quasi-ergodic behaviour in Monte-Carlo simulations by
J-walking: Applications to atomic clusters" by D.D. Franz, D.L. Freeman
and J.D. Doll, J. Chem. Phys. 93, 2769 (1990)]
Instead of calculating such a distribution ahead of time and storing it we run
Monte Carlo simulations at the higher temperatures simultaneously with the
lower-temperature calculations and use PVM to pass the higher-temperature
configurations to the lower temperatures.

Q:How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
A:We are using four Silicon Graphics Indigo workstations.

From: Sowmini Varadhan <varadhan@cs.utk.edu>
> 
> Are you using PVM today?

Yes.

> What are your application(s)?

Parallel numeric computing for the computation of the SVD of
large, sparse matrices. 

> How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

Sparcs, RS6K

> Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.
> Please email the information to pvm-survey@cs.utk.edu.

Some comments on the PVM book, available on-line-

The PVM book leaves much to be desired:
It's not clear what _kind_ of audience this book is targetted for. 
Is it intended for

1. the scientist/engineer who wants to use PVM to implement some algorithm
   in parallel, or

2. the network programmer, who wishes to understand the implementation
   details?

In case 1, description of the implementation details should be intended
only to show how efficiency gains may be achieved. In case 2, implementation
details should show how the applications motivated PVM design.

In either case, Chapter 7 ("How PVM Works") is confusing, and 
appears to be badly organized; while it makes an attempt to describe 
the data structures used to implement buffers, host tables etc., 
there is a recurring problem of cross-references: terms are used 
before they are clearly defined, so that it neither throws light
on the implementation details, nor does it indicate how to use
the libraries to obtain max. efficiency. This chapter needs some 
serious restructuring.

--Sowmini

From: mcastro@dsee.fee.unicamp.br (Marcelo Stehling de Castro)

>Are you using PVM today?

Yes, I am.

>What are your application(s)?

It's an On-line operation and control of power systems using distributed computing environments.

>How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

I am using 3 different kind of machines using 2 architetures : SUN4 and RS6K
which are described bellow:


DCE#1: Sparc2+Ethernet

	This distributed environment consists of ten SUN UNIX-based workstations (one server 470 and nine
 Sparc2 model) connected as an Ethernet LAN (coaxial cable), featuring nominal bandwidth of 10 Mbps.



DCE#2: RS6K/560+Ethernet

	It's an homogeneous cluster of eight IBM RISC/6000 workstations (model 560) interconnected as an 
Ethernet token-ring LAN (coaxial cable) with nominal bandwidth of 16 Mbps.



DCE#3: RS6K/370+FDDI

	The third DCE used for testing is a cluster of eight IBM RISC/6000 workstations (model 370) that 
constitute a SP1 computer (Scalable PowerParallel System 1). Each node has 256 Mbytes of RAM and delivers
 peak performance of 125 Mflops. The nodes are connected as a fiber optic token-ring LAN (Fiber
 Distributed Data Interface/FDDI), running at nominal bandwidth of 100 Mbps, through an active wire 
center (hub).

	NOTES:

	A) DCE#1 is located in Faculty of Electrical Engineering at the University of Campinas, Brazil;

	B) DCE#2 and DCE#3 were part of the High Performance Computing  National Center at S~ao Paulo 
		State (CENAPAD-SP);

From: basilio@udc.es (Basilio Bernardo Fraguela Rodriguez)


 In answer to your polite letter, here are my responses to your questions:


 * Are you using PVM today?

   YES. I am researching with another two persons on the distributed
  execution of programs written in functional languages, and we have
  selected PVM as the ideal software packet to provide the distributed
  execution facilities we need.

  
 * What are your application(s)?

   I started to use PVM working on the distribution of mathematical
  algorithms on a cluster of computers (mainly, matrix products and
  large simulations using different data in each computer, whose
  results where gathered to get global results).

   In our new project, we use the interface facilities of a functional
  language called Caml Light with C. The C functions use PVM to create
  tasks corresponding to modules that act as function servers and to
  perform all the communications needed.

   When a client whishes to perform distributed computations, it enters
  PVM calling a function that registers it in PVM and spawns a number
  of servers specified by the client. Later, when it wants a computation
  to be performed remotely, in a server, it passes all the data needed to
  a C function, which sends them to a job scheduler. The client can
  continue with its own computations, without waiting for the result.
  Later, when the computations performed by the client need the result of
  the remote computation, the client will have to wait for it.
  
   The job scheduler decides which server is to perform the computation
  and sends the data to that server, which will later send the result
  to the client. Servers can also make requests to other servers,
  as we have developed a mechanism to avoid deadlocks.

   If you are interested in knowing more about our project, please do not
  doubt to mail me.


 * How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

   By now we have been using clusters of, at most, 19 Sun SPARCstations ELC.
   For simple trials we use about two or three Sun SPARCstations IPX.
   As you can see they all belong to the SUN4 architecture.

 * Our suggestions.

   We wonder if it would we possible to develop a PVM version capable
  of communicating tasks belonging to different users, as this would
  increase a lot the system flexibility.

   We are also interested in an improvement of the tools to measure
  times and track calls to PVM services. We do think that a lot of
  people is concerned about time measuring, as the reduction in the
  computational times is the real reason for PVM usage.

   Finally we would like to know if there is any forum, congress or
  society dedicated to the study, discussion  and promotion of the
  projects developed using PVM.

  
   Thanks for PVM, we have found it to be a really useful tool.


 +-------------------------------------------+
 |  Basilio B. Fraguela Rodriguez            |
 |  Depto. de Electronica y Sistemas         |
 |  Facultad de Informatica                  |
 |  Campus de Elvinha                        |
 |  15071   La Corunha                       |
 |  Spain                                    |
 |                                           |
 |  (basilio@udc.es)                         |

Are you using PVM today?

What are your application(s)?
  
  Mechanical Engineering, simulation, optimization,

  to powerful tools

How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
 
  HPPA, SGI5, (SGI, R6k, Paragon)
  4-20 machines

----------------------------------------------------------------

Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.

Thank you very much for PVM! A lot of work and some very nice
projects for our students wouldn't have been possible without
this nice, reliable (and cheap) tool.

  But:

- Tracing is VERY BAD. You should support the paragraph-traceformat.
  XPVM is not stable, useless for interactive or big programs and
  has too limited functionality in tracing compared to paragraph. Pablo is
  not easy available on HPPA's and thus no alternative.

- I have to use the hostfile very often to set paths, ... .
  Certainly this info is stored in an internal datastructure. It
  would be a very nice (and maybe simple to realize) feature to 
  get info about the actual options of specific hosts from within
  the pvm console.

- XPVM is based on Tcl/Tk, tools not very stable and not portable
  over their own versions. A simple X or Motif GUI would be
  preferable (Motif is not free, ... -I know).

From: Thomas Erlebach <erlebach@informatik.tu-muenchen.de>

Hi!

>Are you using PVM today?

Yes.

>What are your application(s)?

I'm working on a compiler for a new Pascal-like programming language, APRIL, that
is intended for the easy parallelization of divide and conquer algorithms. The
compiler generates C code which uses PVM for message passing. Example applications
for my compiler (and therefore for PVM, too) include a chip layout algorithm,
a Mandelbrot program, and an algorithm for the travelling salesman problem.

>How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

I've used SUN workstations (Sparc 1, Sparc 2, Sparc 10: architecture SUN4) and
HP 9000/720 workstations (architecture: HPPA). I've used up to 16 SUN's and
up to 70 HP's without problems. We have 110 HP's but I've had serious problems
when I had more than about 70 HP's in the virtual machine. Machines started to drop
out of the virtual machine before I even started an application. I've had
error messages like:

[t80040000] netinput() FIN|ACK from hphalle2j
[t80040000]  hd_dump() ref 1 t840000 n "hphalle2j" ar "HPPA" lo ""
[t80040000]            sa 131.159.4.40:2011 mtu 4096 f 0x0 e 0 txq 0
[t80040000]            tx 9 rx 6 rtt 0.310330

>Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.

In general I've been very satisfied with PVM, except for a few problems. First, I've
had the problem I mentioned above with more than about 70 machines. I guess that
it might be caused by some buffers or other data structures within PVM being
configured too small at our site (I'm not the person who installed PVM here).

Another problem I encountered was that messages got lost when I used the option
PvmRouteDirect and a process terminated (pvm_exit) immediately after sending
a message. I got around it by having the master program send a termination
message (via PvmDontRoute) to all other processes. The other processes wait
for this message before they terminate.

By the way, we're still using PVM 3.2.6 at our site.

>Your help is much appreciated.

I hope I was of assistance.

Keep up the good work!

Thomas Erlebach

-- 
erlebach@informatik.tu-muenchen.de

From: Cristiano Andre da Costa <cac@akira.ucpel.tche.br>

Dear collegue,
	I used PVM until December in a work to finish my undergraduate 
course. The Abstract of my work was:

	Parallel computing has been used to btain a better performance in 
computer systems, as well as a good cost-benefit relation. Nowadays, with 
the sequential computing technology achieving its limit, it becomes more 
important to explore the parallel processing.
	Parallel computing can be explored with the use of software 
environments developed specifically to this goal. Among these 
environments, Parallel Virtual Machine (PVM) can be emphasized. PVM is a 
software system that permits a network of heterogeneous UNIX computers to 
be usde as a single large parallel computer.
	This work intends to use the distributed parallel processing with 
the PVM in a network of IBM RISC/System 6000 workstations. In the study 
of this environment a granularity analysis and a comparison between the 
sequential and parallel processing are included.
	During this work, PVM was intalled at UCPEL (my University), 
organized with samples programas and with a user's manual to help 
researchers who want to use this parallel computing environment.

From: <bocchino@oapa.astropa.unipa.it>

Are you using PVM today?
Yes

What are your application(s)?
2-D Hydrodynamical applications based on FCT scheme (see Reale et al.,
Nuovo Cimento B 105 (1990), 1235.

How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
Array of DECstations 5000 + Ethernet LAN
Array of DEC3000 (based on DEC Alpha processors) + FDDI LAN.

Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.
We investigated the feasibility of using non-dedicated parallel systems
with PVM and concluded that the convenience depends essentially on the size
of the computational domain as compared to the relative processor power and
network bandwidth. We point out the software still offers great opportunities
of improvement, especially in terms of latency times in the message-passing
protocols. In condition of significant gain in terms of speed-up, such
workstation arrays represent a cost-effective approach to massive parallel
computation (see Reale, Bocchino and Sciortino, Comp. Phy. Comm. 83 (1994),
130-140.

>What are your application(s)?

Numerical analysis, predominantly.

>How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

I used to have access to nine HP9000/735-125's on FDDI.

>Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.
>Please email the information to pvm-survey@cs.utk.edu.

I can get pvm to speed up fairly well with a malloc replacement library
my company sells (the Memory Tuning System, or MTS).  First, would the
University be interested in shipping a faster PVM with a portable, much
faster malloc package?  Or, somehow allow us to have a reference out on
netlib or something?  Second, how would one go about getting a copy of
the pvm mailing list in order to see if there are any pvm users that
would be interested?

XPVM is very nice; keep up the good work there!

PVM itself seems to be improving in quality and acceptance over time; my
fear is that it is quickly approaching the point where it has a
sufficiently large user group that we may have to start (gasp :-) paying
for it.

al

From: kalns@canidae.cps.msu.edu

> Are you using PVM today?

The Department of Computer Science (CPS) at Michigan State
University is using PVM, version3.3.5 at the time of this
e-mail.

> What are your application(s)?

There are a variety; here are some representative samples:
1. Workstation cluster work allocation algorithms, PVM used
   for job start/stop and message-passing among nodes.
2. Undergraduate and graduate-level courses in operating systems,
   networking, and parallel systems.
3. Various simulations for distributed-memory machines which require
   extensive inter-processor communication.

> How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

PVM is used on over 200 Sun SPARCs and several DEC Alpha workstations
in our department.

Well, a couple of things........
But, firstly I am not sure if these suggestions have already
been implemented...........so forgive my ignorance....

1. From the slave processor, instead of writing output to
   a temporary file when using 'write(*,*)', at times it would
   be useful to have these written straight to the screen.
   One might have each slave id number before something is written...

2. To be able to choose which machine a slave may use...
   Because, I am not sure how PVM chooses its slaves. Sometimes
   I often wonder why one particular machine is chosen even though
   it has a higher load than another? Could you please reply to this
   question.

3. I would like to know(perhaps visually??) which slaves are waiting
   for data and which are chewing away at the data...

From: kortas@marius.univ-mrs.fr (samuel Kortas)

Hi there!

	Yes I'm using a lot PVM : I am  PhD student
	working on solving the Navier Stokes Equations with some high 
	precision schemes. My target machine is the T3D and the SP2, but
	I debug and program on a RS6000 Station with PVM : it keeps me
	from spending too much time (and money) on the real machines, and
	offers me a nice platform to debug my code.

	Although I use PVM, I wanted to access the shmem memory library of
	the T3D. So, instead of calling PVM directly in my code, I call my
	own subset of (very limited) instructions of communications, which
	call either PVM primitive, either T3D routines on the real machine.
	That way, I think my code stays quite portable and can sustain better
	performance on the T3D.



    pvm-survey> Any comments and suggestions for improvement are
    pvm-survey> welcome.  

	Thank you very much for the great job you do on PVM! 
	
	Would it be possible to have some global function as  a
	global add or global min? 
	Also it would be a blast if we could have a better parallel 
	debugging tool for SPMD programs. I dream of a hack, under
	unix or emacs, to be able to put a breakpoint at a line in
	every similar program of one session PVM... In a word, a
	way of avoiding to have to jump from windows to windows to
	type in the same order in as many dbx windows as there are
	similar tasks running.

    pvm-survey> Best wishes, The PVM Project Team

	Best wishes to you too, and long life to PVM!

From: Michel DAYDE <dayde@enseeiht.fr>

Are you using PVM today?
  The answer is definitively yes...

What are your application(s)?
  We use it both in training and research.

1. Training :
     We use as an example of message-passing programming environment.
We have lectures on introduction to PVM (in our university, but
we do the same lectures in courses that are funded by EEC). We use
it also for demonstrating some of the particular aspects of heterogeneous
computing. The main aspect in the PVM course are hands-on sessions.

2. Research :
   PVm is used for developing parallel codes on distributed memory computers
and clusters of workstations. These parallel codes are sparse codes
(direct and iterative solvers) and computational kernels in linear algebra,
and solution of large scale optimization problems. Note that this involves
collaborations with various labs, espceially CERFACS and RAL.

   WE are also heavily involved in parallelizing industrial codes. For example,
we have parallelized a flutter calculation code for Aerospatiale on
workstation clusters using PVM.
    We also use PVM (and PARMACS) within an ESPRIT project, called
Parallel Aero, funded by EEC. This project concerns the parallelization
of a 3D Navier-Stokes Solver and involve several partners (CERFACS, CIRA,
ENSEEIHT-IRIT, EPFL, RUS, KTH, and industrial partners that use the
code Aerospatiale and SAAB).

How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
    WE run PVM on a large range of workstations : DEC, IBM, HP, SUN
connected by Ethernet, FDDI, or SOCC (only some of these are in-house).
WE use it (or will soon use it) on BBN GP1000 and BBN TC2000, 
CRAY T3D, KSR1, and CONVEX Exemplar.


Sincerely yours,
      Michel Dayde,
      ENSEEIHT-IRIT

~c dayde

From: thomas.bahls@stud.uni-rostock.de (Thomas Bahls)
:
:Are you using PVM today?

Yes, I am. In general, I use it about three times a week.

:What are your application(s)?

self written ones (mostly Master-Slave applications) and several so called 
Basic Linear Algebra Routines (e.g. ScaLapack, currently I try to install it)

:How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

homogenous RS/6000 cluster of 16 machines (including 9 workstations)

:Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.

In my eyes, PVM is in a state that is nearly more user-friendly and
reliable (in terms of bugs or stability) than most other commercial
software. One very important aspect is the documentation. At our department,
the name "Jack Dongarra" stands for high quality meanwhile.
The documentation isn't only useful as a reference. It's easy to understand
and quite a new PVM user will be well prepared after reading it.
So far the good things...

There are some additional remarks for my private use of PVM.
I am connected via an Ethernet with some other PC's running Linux. We got
installed PVM 3.3 successfully. But there was little trouble compared to the
installation at our RS/6000 cluster.
Furthermore, there are some small problems using PVM at home. We all have
exported /usr/local/bin/pvm3 or mounted it with NFS at the same location.
Unfortunately we need to add the dx (?) statement to add another machine to
our configuration. That's somehow annoying because we all use the same
domain name and the same location. And what's more, we cannot start pvmgs
anyway.

Summarizing it, it may be useful to spend some time on the Linux users of PVM.


:Best wishes,

same to you !

Best regards, 
Thomas.

From: <mubin@wein02.elektro.uni-wuppertal.de>

Dear Sir,

Information about my applications:

1. I am using PVM3.3 today. I have used PVM for one year.

2. My main research interest lies in parallel algorithms 
   for solving linear equations on workstation cluster. 
   The results are expected to be used in the simulation 
   of large electrical networks.

3. I use three DECstation 5000 workstations connected 
   through Ethernet.


Comments and suggestions:

My experience shows that PVM is relatively portable and 
compatible; it is easy to learn and use. It is a good 
parallel programming platform for workstation clusters. 
However, the user wants to have a much clear PVM user's 
guide, especially, clear and sufficient information about 
the commands (Appendix A. Reference pages for PVM3.3 
routines).

Best wishes,

Mubin

e-mail: mubin@wein02.elektro.uni-wuppertal.de

Hi!

 > Are you using PVM today?
We are using PVM in some parts of our graduation thesis. The biggest
part was to analyse if it was possible to use a number of workstations,
running PVM over a ordinary network, as a large parallel machine in the 
parallel computation courses.

I have to admit that our resuls are a bit depressing. In short, we need
a lot faster network to be able to using the workstations as a parallel 
machine.

We will also use PVM later when converting a CONLAB-compiler from using
PICL to PVM. CONLAB is an environmemt to devolp parallel algorithms in
a MATLAB like notation.

testprograms.

ethernet network. If the time admit we will run on Sun:s and SGI indy:s, too.
If we use all machines with approximately equal computation-power we will be 
using 30-40 computers.

From: schiotz@fysik.dtu.dk (Jakob Schiotz)
 > Are you using PVM today?

Not any longer, I switched to use the native message passing system.

 > 
 > What are your application(s)?
 > 

Analysis of Molecular Dynamics simulations

 > How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
 > 

Mostly a CM-5E, but also Sun SPARC workstations

 > Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.
 > Please email the information to pvm-survey@cs.utk.edu.
 > 

The reason I "left" PVM is that I was running a Master/Slave program
on a CM-5 where most communication was between the master and the
slave.  Using CMSSL the communication goes like this:

	[Master (Front end)]	<--->  [Slave (Node)]

With PVM:

	[Master (F.E.)] <---> [pvmd (F.E.)] <---> 
		[PVM Host program (F.E.)] <---> [Slave (Node)]

And, even worse: The Master could send data so fast that pvmd couldn't
pass it on fast enough, so it grew and grew until memory became very
short.

But I must say that I am glad that I made the program in PVM first.
Debugging on our local workstations probably more than halved the
developing time, and then it was very easy to port the working
application to CMSSL.  If I am ever again going to write a message
passing program on a MMP, I'll seriously consider writing and
debugging it in PVM, and then port it if necessary.

Thanks for making PVM available.

Jakob Schiotz                    !  Center for Atomic-scale 
CAMP, Physics Department         !  Materials Physics (CAMP):
Technical University of Denmark  !  
DK-2800 Lyngby, Denmark          !  http://www.fysik.dtu.dk/
schiotz@fysik.dtu.dk             !

From: destri@otello (Giulio Destri)

 From: Dr. Giulio Destri, PhD Student
       Dipartimento di Ingegneria dell'Informazione    
       Universita' degli Studi di Parma              
       43100 Parma - Italy

 TO:
 PVM Project Team
 pvm-survey@cs.utk.edu

Dear Colleagues,

We apologize for our late in answering. Here you can find our answer
(and some question).

> Are you using PVM today?
Here at our departement we are starting now to using PVM.

> What are your application(s)?
I am a PhD student in Computer Engineering and my Interests are
Application of Parallel and Distributed systems to Computer
Vision problems.
I work together with Paolo Marenzoni,
another PhD student, whose interests are
Massive Parallel Systems performance study and analisys and
Petri Nets, and with some undergraduate students,
Stefano Brozzi, Andrea Menozzi and Cristina Molinari.
Our interests are fundamentally two:
1. Using the PVM to obtain a MIMD distributed solution for
   very big Petri Nets.
2. The use of PVM to integrate some distributed Image Processing
   tools, expecially AVS.
    We read on the Web page of Computer Graphics Unit of
    Manchester Computing Centre, University of Manchester,
    United Kingdom the summaries of the results of the Summer
    Projects made at Computer Graphics Unit in 1993 and 1994 and we
    think that the following two projects are particularly interesting:

      1) Andrew Banks (1993) " A 30-page tutorial on parallel AVS "

      2) David Bancroft (1994) " Parallel AVS on HP/Silicon Graphics using PVM "

    We would like to know if more information about these projects, or
    about others concerning these arguments, are available via ftp or Web
    (we were unable to find them on Web pages) or if at least you can mail
    us the involved people's E-mail (if they have one) so that we can contact
    them directly.

> How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
We have installed PVM v. 3.3.6
on a series of SPARC stations with various processors
and memory configurations, and we have encountered some problems.
To save disk space we have installed PVM in the directory /usr/local/pvm3,
setting correctly the PVM_ROOT and PVM_ARCH environment variables.
1. The compilation under SOLARIS 2.0 stops, with some library not found
   complain.
2. Under SunOS 4.1.2 all seem to work, but not always.
3. Under SunOS 4.1.3 we have some problems at run time, i.e. the spawn
   does not always work, with no apparent cause.
4. When we tried to install (unpacking the tar file) the HeNCE program
   some strange link errors (i.e. ldopen not found...) appeared in the
   successive compilations.

Could you help us to solve these problems?

Thanks in advance.

Best Regards,

                Giulio Destri     (destri@ce.unipr.it)
                Paolo Marenzoni   (marenz@ce.unipr.it)
                Stefano Brozzi    (brozzis@ce.unipr.it)
                Andrea Menozzi    (menozzia@ce.unipr.it)
                Cristina Molinari (molicri@ce.unipr.it)

     > Are you using PVM today?

Yes.

     > What are your application(s)?

I am currently developing a program to solve spin waves.  Simulating a
piece of magnetic tape as a pseudo 2-D surface of vectors(rods)
pointing in the direction of the rods spin axis.  There is heavy
communication between neighbor rods and the size of the blocks to
break the computation into needs to be optimized.  Space parallization
is all I have implemented so far, but I hope to get far enough to also
implement time parallization methods with multigrid.  But development
is going slow.

From: "Dr.Blaszczyk (Dr.Bl)" <ab@decrc.abb.de>

Dear Colleagues,

Here are some answers to your pvm-survey-questions.


Are you using PVM today?

   Yes.

What are your application(s)?

   We developed parallel solver for 3D electrostatic field calculations
   This solver is used also by designers of high voltage insulation in ABB 
   The parallel computation with PVM allow to use the existing hardware
   and to achieve the speed up of the design process. The software is used 
   by R&D departments in production sites as well as in ABB Corporate
   Research Centers. 

How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

   We are using workstation clusters including Sun, IBM RS6k, and HP 700.
   Our application is not very dependent from the communication speed
   so we can use standard ethernet for communication (provided that it
   is not overloaded) We are currently  using not more than 10 workstations
   in a cluster. An important problem for us is good reliability of 
   calculations in heterogeneous clusters - the calculation must go on 
   even if one of workstations fails.
   We are going now to implement our solver for IBM SP2.

Best Regards

A. Blaszczyk

From: Parallel VM <pvm@risc.uni-linz.ac.at>

Dear Colleagues,

I am glad to answer to your questions.

Yes - I am currently using PVM (though, to say the truth, I am considering the
possibility to reconfigure the applications towards the MPI standard).

The use of PVM concerns a parallel distributed kernel for a C++ math library;
such a kernel provides basic primitives for local and remote activation of
parallel tasks. The thread-based nature of the library is somehow conflicting
with the non-reentrancy of the PVM code; this is one of the main reasons for
considering a passage to MPI.

At the moment, PVM is used in a test version of the library, running on a
Sequent Symmetry machine. Very soon we plan to export the library to a set
of Silicon Graphics workstations. The final step will be exporting it to an
SP-2 environment - but this will take some time.

Hope it is useful. Best wishes,

  Piergiorgio Bertoli

  pbertoli@risc.uni-linz.ac.at
  pvm@risc.uni-linz.ac.at

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From: Clayton Heller <cheller@uni-sw.gwdg.de>

To whom it may concern,

In regards to your request for information on PVM usage:

I have developed an interactive orbit analysis code which uses 
version 3 of PVM.  It finds, as a function of energy, all of the 
characteristic periodic orbits in a rotating non-axisymmetric 
potential and determines their
stability.  It will also produce, for a given energy,  a phase space
map showing the regions of stability and chaos.  This information is
used to understand gas flows in barred galaxies.  The algorithm
uses a fairly sophisticated load balancing scheme which allows for
efficient operation in a heterogeneous environment with processors
of widely varying speed and load.  It is also robust in the sense that
the loss of processors during the run will not affect the computation.

I have been running at the University of Kentucky (for about three years)
on a collection of
Sun, HP, and Decstation workstations.  Unfortunately, since my arrival
in Gottingen Germany I have not been able to get PVM to work on a
network of Dec Alphas.  Version 3.2.6 would not compile on one machine,
compiled on another but would not spawn the pvm deamons.  I installed
3.2.5 and got it to compile and start up, but it would not start 
my slave processes (just froze).  As I have been busy on other things
lately, I have not tried anything else or contacted anyone.  I will try
again later this month and if I still have trouble will e-mail your
group for help.

Clayton Heller

From: "Leszek Opalski p254B t7877" <OPALSKI@ipe.pw.edu.pl>

Yes, I am using PVM with my student for speeding up multiple 
simulation of electronic circuits. The need arises eg. when we perform 
statistical performance evaluation of a circuit, or do optimization. 
In our applications certain number of circuit analyses are needed 
before a decision is made (by an algorithm or by a human). Parameters 
for these analysis can differ slightly (eg. in sensitivity analysis) 
or substancially (eg. in Monte Carlo). We try to deal with both 
situations, although so far the second is investigated more. We 
have plans for using PVM for speeding up simulations related to 
noise phenomena in circuits.
We use PVM on different SparcStation machines of Sun (with single 
CPU) under Solaris2. PVM serves us as an interface standard for 
distributed programming and as a quality library that implements that 
standard. So far we have not experimented with fine-grain 
parallelization, because of our hardware, but it is good to 
know it is there when we have resources and a need.

Thank you for releasing the package to the public,

            Dr Leszek Opalski
            The Institute of Electronics Fundamentals
            Warsaw University of Technology
            Warsaw, Poland.

From: John Holdzkom <holdzkom@ccpo.odu.edu>

I do not currently use PVM, although I may resume using it
in the future.

It was used in a particle-in-cell model for simulations of 
mesoscale features, such as eddies and coastal fronts in 
oceanography.

PVM was mostly used on a network of Sun workstations, although
some experimentation was done with PVM on a Cray T3D.

At this time, our problem does not require PVM.  We found that
each workstation finished its task quickly, while packing, sending,
and receiving messages consumed more time.  Network traffic was
a major culprit of this.

From: Dan Fox <fox@vulcan.nrlssc.navy.mil>

I recently received a query from you about our PVM usage.  I've
been out sick, so hopefully this is not too late!


Are you using PVM today?
	
	Yes.

What are your application(s)?

	1. Distributed version of the POVRAY raytracer.  We generate
	   a large number of raytraced scenes for scientific visualization
	   and occasionally use a PVM-ized version of the code which was
	   done by Brad Kline at Cray (patches available at ftp.povray.org)

	2. A C language extension called "Glenda" was built on top of
	   PVM.  For "normal" users, this greatly eases the overhead
	   involved in learning PVM.  Using Glenda (and therefore
	   indirectly using PVM), I wrote some codes to examine the
	   efficiency of using the local Sun network to do some tasks
	   like optimal interpolation.  These are mostly toy codes so
	   far though.

	3. In the works:  one of our contractors is writing a PVM-ized
	   version of an ocean circulation model.  The goal is to have
	   a code which will run on the T3D, SP2, and local Sun network
	   as needed.

How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

	Successful:  a network of Suns of various types (mostly
		Sparc2, 10, and 20's)

	Unsuccessful:  between a Sparc10 and a Cray YMP.  

Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.

	Some method of load balancing would be useful.  I
	try to use agenda methods to divide up problems so that
	slow machines end up doing fewer parts, but this is not
	always possible.  Ideally (and this would be asking a lot!)
	some sort of process migration where jobs would "shift"
	to idle machines would be available.

 in this survey and contribute to your project (some results from our 

 experience with it), as it appears to be a quiet usefull one.

  Here are the answers to your 3 questions:

 1.  Yes, we are using PVM for the last few months. we're evaluating the usage

   in terms of Total Time Consumption when making our computations, and so far 

   the results are quiet promising, showing improvements that fit our needs.

 2.  The main application we use with PVM was developed in our company (Israel

   Electric Corporation  - Research & Development department).

     This application is using changing sets of restrains and field-conditions

   to plan an "annual time-schedule for all maintenance operations" in power-stations

   and power-units all over the country.

 3.  We are using different numbers of machines each time, depending upon the "load"

   on machines and through our network. We've checked this system upto 16 machines

   simoultaneuously (it looks o.k.) but for getting good results, we've experienced

   that 6 to 9 machines are better and sometimes even less (this is influenced also

   by our network conditions).

     The important issue, from our point of view, is that we are using mixed 

   combinations of: 
			Decstations 5000/240 (running Ultrix 4.3)
			&
			Digital Alpha work-stations (running OSF 1.3 or 1.2).

From: Henrik Lauf Christensen <lauf@iesd.auc.dk>

During the last semester I have participated in a group where we have made an
evaluation of PVM.

In doing this we have made two application and some synthetic benchmarks. The
two application benchmarks were:

	1: Raytracing. This was done by putting a PVM-shell around POV-ray.
	  The achieved speedup was 19.

	2: Game of Life. The achieved speedup was 26 with a large board
	  consisting of 2000x2000 squares. With smaller boards the speedup
	  was below 1, mainly due to poor performance of Ethernet.

The conclusion for the application benchmarks were, that PVM is only suited for
coarse-grained applications, because communication over network is *very* slow.
We had no particulary load balancing, and belive a more efficient load balan

...continuing broken mail.

cing would have increased the achieved speedup somewhat.

The synthetic benchmarks were designed to measure the performance of PVM's
message-passing via Ethernet and found that PVM introduced some overhead in
the magnitude of 2 to 5 times.

We have around 120 SUN workstations available at the campus running SUN4 and
SUN4SOL2. We experineced some problems when trying to connect more than 50
workstations. We either could not add more machines or we lost connection to
them. Wheter this was due to the many experiments on the workstations and the
network or PVM, we do not know.

(speedup in the two application benchmarks was achieved with 50 workstations).


best wishes

lauf@iesd.auc.dk

From: teompf@garm.teokem.lu.se (Markus Fulscher)

   Dear Colleague,

   I am a member of the department of Theoretical Chemistry at the 
   University of Lund (Sweden). Recently, we started a project aiming
   at the parallelization of our programs - the software package is 
   called MOLCAS and is available for various machines. The goal is
   to rewrite the programs in such a way that they can be run on 
   distributed as well as shared memory machines. The specific 
   architectures we have in mind are heterogeneous networks such as
   clusters of work stations, the IBM/SP2 and SGI's parallel work stations.
   As PVM is de facto a standard running almost any UNIX based computers 
   it is the natural choice to solve the communication problem. Moreover, 
   as IBM, SGI and other vendors offer machine specific implementations 
   of PVM tuned for maximum efficiency portability is granted. 

   An other standard that may be used to reach our goal is MPI.
   At present we think, however, MPI is to complex to be used in
   a straight forward way. Moreover, to my knowledge not to many 
   vendors offer products based on the MPI standard.
   
   As PVM is a rather simple tool it misses several features of 
   importance with respect to the development of new codes such as
   powerful monitors to watch the performance of the program. Because
   of that we are using IBM's PE which is based on the MPI standard
   as a development toolkit (a transparent interface is under 
   development).
   
   M. Fuelscher

From: stefan.nonneman@jrc.it (Stefan Nonneman)

Dear Colleague,

As You asked in Your e-mail of 6-1-1995, I send You the answers on the
questions related to what we are 
doing with PVM.

1. We intend to use PVM this days. It is not Yet installed. I started
studying the reference guide, in order to make me familiar  with the
concept.

2. I'm working in the nuclear world, doing Monte-Carlo simulations with the
code MCNP developed by
ORNL and LANL. An option of this code is that it is modified in a way
permitting to run the code under PVM. In my present day work I need to
tackle two types of problems. In order to perform optimisation studies, I
need calculation power of the scale of huge main frame in order to perform
the runs in a suitable period of time. The solution is a large number of
machines in a distributed systems management system ( with AMD tech for
distribution of file systems ) and a script starting the code once a
previous run is finished. A second type of problems is the one where I need
to run once the code but with an enormous number of particles. Here PVM is
very helpful.

3. For the moment I have only 13 Sparc 10 and 20 machines available under
Solaris 1.1.1. In our institute I have access to a Dec - Alfa and probably
also to a HP 9000/735. As a first test I want to use only the Sun stations.

If You need more information please ask me.

From: <mehaut@lifl.fr>

-->Are you using PVM today?

Yes, every day we use PVM! My team is one of the Computer Science Lab of Lille
(LIFL).

-->What are your application(s)?

PVM is a good support for:

	for Parallel and Irregular Applications 
        (Branch&Bound, Parallel Genetic Alg., Quadratic Affectation...)

	for the design of cooperating applications.
	(PVM is used for the Communication Library)

	for Students in the "Parallel Programming" module.
	(100 students learn and use PVM)


We use a Multithreaded approach for the parallel and distributed 
programming. (like TPVM, Athapascan (IMAG)...). 

Several others teams use PVM for

	Data Parallel Programming (Data Parallel Language MPL [Maspar] is ported on PVM)

	Graphical team (Parallel Ray Casting program with PVM)

 
-->How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

Research Lab.
------------

16 DEC_ALPHA (FARM)
10 SUN4
4  SUN4SOL2 (Sparc Classic)
4  SUN4SOL2 (Sparc 5)
1  SUNMP (Sparc 10, biprocessor)
10 PCLINUX (486 DX-2 66)

We also use the IBM SP1 of Grenoble (IMAG, apache team) (32 processors)

Students classroom.
------------------

1  SUNMP (Sparc 10, biprocessor)
1  SUN4 (Sparc 2)
16 SUN4 (Sparc IPC)
8  SUN4 (Sparc ELC)
24 SUN4SOL2 (Sparc Classic)
24 PCLINUX (486 DX-2 66)


-->Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.

We had some difficulties to use the Multithreaded library on PVM.
Because we wanted a Preemptive execution with priorities, we had some
difficulties because the PVM kernel is not MT-SAFE (Multithreading safe).
We modified the PVM library and protected the critical, global and
shared data (for example the message buffers...).

The students appreciated PVM, because the model is very simple to understand
and they "easily" build real parallel program. But student often make mistakes
and the debugging is difficult.

Best regards and happy new year to the PVM team!

JF Mehaut

From: Stefan Rottegger <rottegge@informatik.tu-muenchen.de>
> 
> Are you using PVM today?
yes

Nothing speciell.
I'm working on a visualistion tool for pvm and I need only
trace data for tests. So my applications do nothing beside
using every avaiable pvm function.
> 
> How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
SUN4, LINUX
> 
> Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.
The order of receiving data is not correct.
In the case one task is direct linked with for example taskA
and another task isn't, I detected the following problem:
If the direct linked task sends first
and taskA receives (with wildcards)  after the send of the two tasks,
taskA gets the message of the direct linked task second.
(the sending tasks must be on different machines than the receiving
 task).

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
From: keith@supr.scm.liv.ac.uk (Keith Taylor)

Dear PVM Project Team,

   Although aware of PVM's existence for some time, I had not used it in
anger until last November, when I employed it as the basis for a short course
on parallel programming. I was most impressed! Its major strengths, as I see
it are:

1. it is available on a great variety of machines and architectures, making 
   it the most portable message passing system that I know;

2. it is easy to set up; I obtained it by email and installed it on a network 
   of Silicon Graphics workstations from scratch, with the minimum of fuss; a
   PC running LINUX was later added with no problems;

3. PVM is extremely well documented; I borrowed freely from the user's guide
   for the course;

4. the examples provided are a good basis for practical workshops, but could
   have to be tidied a little.

   I have one major criticism. The mechanism for sending and receiving seems
at first, at least, extremely clumsy. Is there a good reason that send and
receive procedures cannot be pointed at user created buffers rather than the
implicit current send and receive buffers?

   I hope my comments have been of some assistance.


Yours sincerely,

Keith Taylor

From: <gabuaa@bepc2.ihep.ac.cn>

Dear Colleague:
	I have received your email about pvm survey.Thank for your email.I have a 
pleasure to answer your three questions , and I want to send an improved aimk
file to you.I hope that you will send me some new information about PVM in the 
future.

First, I answer your questions:
1) Are you using PVM today?
  Yes,I am using PVM3.3.5. 

2) What are your application(s)?
  Our applications are scientifical computing and its visualization.

3) How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
  Our project is called "Scalable Parallel Clusters System".We have used six 
SPARCstion 2 and 10 with PVM. We will use eight heterogeneous machines which
consists of SPARCstation2 ,SPARCstation 10,SGI and Intel Pentium PC with PVM.

Second,I used aimk to compile PVM programs,when I gave make file a name 
"makefile.aimk",the compiling fails.It would pass only if the make file was 
named "Makefile.aimk". So I modified the aimk file in order to succeed in 
compiling PVM programs by name "Makefile.aimk" or "makefile.aimk" on Nov.4 ,
1994.I send the fellowing improved aimk file to you .

 Best wishes for the PVM Project Team!

 Wu Xingfu 

 1/18/95

Note:I added B shell sentences between "****" and "****" in aimk file. I am a 
PH.D student in department of computer science and engneering ,Beijing 
University of Aeronautics and Astronautics ,Beijing 100083, P.R.China.

The fellowing is the improved aimk file:

makeincwd=0
found=1
while [ $# -ge 1 -a $found = 1 ]; do
	found=0
	case "$1" in
	-here ) makeincwd=1; shift; found=1 ;;
	esac
done

case "x$PVM_ROOT" in x )
		echo aimk: PVM_ROOT not defined >&2
		exit 1
;; esac

case "x$PVM_ARCH" in x | xUNKNOWN )
	PVM_ARCH="`$PVM_ROOT/lib/pvmgetarch`"
	case "x$PVM_ARCH" in x )
		echo 'aimk: no pvmgetarch - is $PVM_ROOT set correctly?' >&2
		exit 1
	;; esac
;; esac

export PVM_ARCH
export PVM_ROOT

#
# run make in cwd or subdir if exists.
#

if [ $makeincwd = 0 -a \( -f $PVM_ARCH/Makefile -o -f $PVM_ARCH/makefile \) ]; then
	echo making in $PVM_ARCH/ for $PVM_ARCH
	cd $PVM_ARCH
	exec make PVM_ARCH=$PVM_ARCH $@

else

# Add the fellowing two lines
#****************************************************
	while [ -f Makefile.aimk -o -f makefile.aimk ]
	do
#****************************************************
	if [ -f Makefile.aimk ]; then
		if [ ! -d $PVM_ARCH ]; then
			mkdir $PVM_ARCH
		fi
		echo making in $PVM_ARCH/ for $PVM_ARCH
		cd $PVM_ARCH
		exec make -f $PVM_ROOT/conf/$PVM_ARCH.def  -f ../Makefile.aimk PVM_ARCH=$PVM_ARCH $@
	else

#Add the fellowing eight lines
#****************************************************
		if [ ! -d $PVM_ARCH ]; then
			mkdir $PVM_ARCH
		fi
		echo making in $PVM_ARCH/ for $PVM_ARCH
		cd $PVM_ARCH
		exec make -f $PVM_ROOT/conf/$PVM_ARCH.def  -f ../makefile.aimk PVM_ARCH=$PVM_ARCH $@
	fi
	done
#****************************************************
fi

exit 1

From: "Rick Lind" <rick@aem.umn.edu>

I am currently using pvm.

I am doing research in robust control.  I use pvm for implementing parallel
algorithms used in robust control problems.  These types of algorithms
include optimization, controller formulation, and analysis problems.
Research utilizing large flexible space structures leads to robust control
problems of extremely high order that prohibit their being solved on a 
standard workstation with a sequential algorithm.  I am investigating parallel
versions of some of these algorithms for a practical engineering environment
that consists of several workstations without access to a dedicated parallel
supercomputer.  Pvm is the communication software for this research.

The machines in use are 8 Sun and 4 SGI workstations.

rick@aem.umn.edu

From: Ludek Matyska <ludek@ics.muni.cz>

Dear PVM team,

my appologies for the delay, but here is our survey answer:

> Are you using PVM today?
Yes.
> 
> What are your application(s)?
In house developed D-CICADA program (published in J. Comp. Chem., Vol 7, 1994,
presented at the 1st European Conference on Computational Chemistry
at Nantes, France, June 1994).
D-CICADA(FT) -- robust implementation of D-CICADA (presented at 1st
European PVM Users Group Meeting, Roma, Italy, October 1994).
PVM is also used as a basis implementation environment in the research
project involving paralelization of sequential algorithms in
computational chemistry (with the cooperation of some Masters and PhD
degree students).
> 
> How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
Twenty (?). SUN's, (old) DEC (running Ultrix), PC with Linux or BSD/386,
recently Indy from SGI (POWER Challenge from SGI will be our next step).
> 
> Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.
We will enjoy any development in the area of the debugging support. The
debugging becomes the most difficult part of the whole development cycle
(and it is a heavy burden in our environment, where PVM is mostly used as
a tools for experimental computational chemistry). We would like to have
some possibilities to inspect the actual state of the PVM (messages,
buffers, ...), to log the transactions (to be inspected later) and so on.

On the other hand we are very gratefull for having the PVM -- it is
really very good pice of code and even as it is under continuous
development, it is very stable and usefull even when used for large and
long computations. Thank you.

					Ludek Matyska

Faculty of Informatics
and
Institute of Computer Science
Masaryk University
Buresova 20
602 00 Brno				Fax: ++42-5-41212747
Czech Republic				Phone: ++42-5-41321237 ext. 384
e-mail: ludek@ics.muni.cz		       ++42-5-740267

Are you using PVM today?

What are your application(s)?

  The application is coarse-grained parallelization of the DDSCAT code
  by Draine & Flatau.  This code uses finite element techniques to model
  electromagnetic scattering properties of arbitrarily-shaped interstellar
  dust grains.  At some stage we may also attempt parallelization of the
  FFT part of the code.

  PVM DDSCAT code on workstation clusters.  I am joining him on the project 
  to try implementation on the Cray T3D at Pittsburgh; this parallel machine
  consists of 256 DEC-Alpha nodes connected in a 3-D torus geometry.

From: Dirk Evers <dirk@TechFak.Uni-Bielefeld.DE>

Hello!

We are evaluating PVM for use as a sublayer to a
high-level communication interface in a Multi Agent System Environment.
Special interest is in the group server facilities.
Questions concern realtime constraints like max. time limits for
messagepassing under heavy cpu load, different communicationmodes,
changes in net-topography at runtime and use of heterogenous architectures.

The Project is called MAKS "Multiagenten-Kommunikations-Subsystem"
and will have to provide flexible message formats and group-communication
while choosing and instanciating agents best suited to solve given tasks.
I will start coding for this project in about 2 months time.
Thanks for a really nice system.

From: <Pascale.Noyret@cerfacs.fr>

Hello 

First sorry for my bad english.

I use pvm for a cooperative projet which
goal is to couple an atmospheric and an Oceanic
General Circulation Models on two distant Cray.

The two Cray are ip-connected through Renater
which is the french network for research and education
(34 Mb/s). One of the Cray was connected to Renater
through an fddi ring and then an ethernet network
and the other through an hippi switch and then ethernet
network.

While sending messages over than 200 reals a time, pvm
expired apparently due to time-out. It was not
so obvious to know it was due to a too big fragmentation
of frames send and that we had to adjust UPDMAXLENGTH
and to recompile pvm.
It is a pity that pvm is not able to know which networks are 
used and to have UDPMAXLENGTH correctly set but I guess
it is not easy to program.  You should perhaps  explain
better how to set UDPMAXLENGTH in documentation.

Best Regards

From: Angel Perles <aperles@pleione.cc.upv.es>

Dear PVM Project Team,


This mail is the reply to yours questions about our use of PVM.

>Are you using PVM today?

We use PVM in order to know the performance of this type of
environments in the development of concurrent discrete time
for the stadistical analysis of the output using replications method.

>What are yor application?

Our test application is based on SMPL discrete time simulator. The
application uses three kinds of processes: a user interface, a 
server daemon that controls replications, and N concurrent replications
(instrumented in order to transfer their status to daemon). Simulation
ends when the user-especified end conditions are reached.

Whe are planning to use this method in more complex simulators.

>How many and what kind of machines have you used whith PVM?

We are using 5 HP9000/735, connected through a FDDI network.

>... sugestions ...

We think that would be interesting to add a library for made easy the
load analysis of hosts in the virtual machine.


Congratulations  for PVM.

From: <BZook%ElectSys%SwRI15@D15VS178A.SPACE.SwRI.EDU>

Dear Colleague,

Here is my response to the recently posted PVM survey.

*** Are you using PVM today? ***

Yes

*** What are your application(s)? ***

a) We have parallelized (using PVM) our finite-difference time-domain (FDTD) 
electromagnetic modeling code using domain decomposition; each slave takes a 
partition of the problem.  It is essentially a data-parallel algorithm, 
requiring us to communicate values between adjacent slaves at their interfaces 
(face, edge, or corner) every timesteps.  Despite the large amount of 
communication, it parallelizes quite well, mainly because communication 
increases with the surface area of the problem space while the computations 
scale as the volume.

b) We have parallelized a couple of our geophysical modeling programs that model 
wave propagation between boreholes.  The calculations are done in the frequency 
domain.  Each frequency is independent, so we parallelize on frequency using the 
 master/slave model; as a slave finishes calculating the result at one 
frequency, it is given another frequency to compute - easy load-balancing.  
After broadcasting global variables at the beginning of the run, only 3 numbers 
are communicated for each frequency.

*** How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM? ***

a) For the FDTD simulation, we have a single code which we have used on: IBM 
RS/6000, HP9000-700 series, SPARC2, SPARCserver 630MP, iPSC/860, and CM-5. This 
software works best on a homogeneous virtual machine.

b) For the geophysical applications, we regularly use a heterogeneous virtual 
machine consisting of 4 workstations: HP9000-433, HP9000-720, SPARC2 (one node 
of a 4-processor SPARCserver 630MP), and an old Sun4/260.

---
Brian Zook
Southwest Research Institute
San Antonio, Texas
bzook@swri.edu
210-522-3630

From: mholin@bla.robin.de (Michael Holin)
>
> Are you using PVM today?

No. I used it for my diploma in computer science.

> What are your application(s)?

I wrote a parallel FFT algorithm for greyscaled images.

> How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

It runned on a network of 4 DEC Alpha and 3 DEC decstations.

> Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.

Debugging the code on the slaves was quite uggly.
And the memory consumption was very high. I had to transfer pieces
of images to and from the slaves. It seems that pvm buffers the
data 2 or 3 times, so that the slaves often had to swap, which
caused the algorithm to work fast only on quite small images.

But nevertheless, a great piece of code.

> Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.

SUGGESTION:

Functions to manipulate
contents/messages of send/received buffers like:
(1) prepend data to the active send buffer;
(2) concatenation of two packed messages from
    two send buffer;
(3) additional unpacking EXTRACT procedure(s)
    I mean,
    if user unpacks something from receive buffer
    then this part of message is EXTRACTED from
    buffer with following consequence:
	(a) as a result of extraction, message has been changed,
	(b) length of message in buffer has been decreased.

QUESTION
	Have you PVM for multiprocessors with transputers, in particular
	Parsytec GC, etc.?

From: ajohnson@math.ukans.edu (Aaron M. Johnson)

     > Are you using PVM today?

Yes.

     > What are your application(s)?

A undergraduate research project in numerical analysis with
Dr. Ben Leimkuhler at the University of Kansas. I am currently
developing a program to solve spin waves.  Simulating a piece of
magnetic tape as a pseudo 2-D surface of vectors(rods) pointing in the
direction of the rods spin axis.  There is heavy communication between
neighbor rods and the size of the blocks to break the computation into
needs to be optimized.  Space parallization is all I have implemented
so far, but I hope to get far enough to also implement time
parallization methods with multigrid.

my experience is limited.

From: Patrick TESSIER <ptessier@matra-ms2i.fr>

We are currently developping a CASE tool that allow developper to
graphically specify
their parallel application program in such a way to define software objects
and communications between them.

The goal of that tool is to be able to fully describe the software without any
hardware deifnition nor constraints.

The hardware that will run the application software is also graphically define
such as processors boards connected on various kind of buses or hardware
platform. For example, you are able to specify a hardware composed of
multiple VME boards with one of them connected as a node to a PVM
bus together with a parallel supercomputer such as CAPITAN using message
passing communication and so on.

Code generators are part of the CASE tool and create the appropiate code
to run and to make all the software object (seen as subroutines) to communicate
together using the hardware platform that has been drawed.

Communication code is as close as the one a developper will have developped
by hand for the hardware he designed.

In such a tool, PVM is one of the communication system known by the
CASE tool along with direct shared memory communication or CAPITAN communication
primitives and others.

Our applications are mainly image and signal processing and use Real time
parallel system.
The CASE tool is a real time application specifier.

To day we have validate the PVM platform in our tool on SUN4 only, but we
plan to use other kind of Unix platform in the near future.

I hope that theses informations will be of some interest for you
and i still available for more detailed information on the CapCASE tool
product if you need it.

The CAPITAN/CapCASE project Team

Patrick TESSIER  MATRA CAP Systemes (33 1) 34 63 72 45
                              Fax:  (33 1) 34 63 72 50

From: ismisa@wi.uni-muenster.de (Mika Saastamoinen)

Well, hi to you too! :)

>In order to improve PVM we are trying to understand how
>people are using the system. Your feedback is important.
>Could you take a moment to answer three questions.

Sure, no problem. I would be very interested in the results as well. When will 
they be ready? 

>  Are you currently using PVM?

Yes, sort of. I'm just "evaluating" (i.e. experimenting with) it as a school 
project. That's why I'd be interested in the results of this survey. I'd like 
to mention in my own project report what sort of things people are using PVM 
for.

>  What are your application(s)?

Just a simple Mandelbrot fractal generator. The image is generated by 
identical slave processes running in parallel, each slave computing a 128x128 
pixel block of the image. The master program collects the blocks, displays 
them to the user and takes care of user I/O. Works very nicely, cool 
pictures... :)

>  How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

Well, I could use upto about 30-35 machines, but usually I use about a dozen 
machines. Most of them are SUN4SOL2s with a couple SUN4s and a few RS6Ks. 
SUN4SOL2s are in the local institute LAN, so I normally use just those, the 
rest are in the wider university network and usually too "crowded" to be worth 
adding to my PVM.

>  Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.

Well, I can't think of anything right now, I'll let you know if I come up with 
something. As a general comment, though, I have to say that PVM is a great 
piece of software, works just great! Keep it up! 

>Your help is much appreciated.

No problemo...

>Best wishes,
>The PVM Project Team

From: <hdc@ctrhdc2.CT.ornl.gov>


We use PVM on rs6k workstations to develop message passing programs for 
molecular dynamics and Monte Carlo simulations of fluids and amorphous 
materials. We later run the codes on SP2 machines (at ORNL and Maui) and

     I have also tried (and failed) to use PVM on an Intel paragon.
There appears to be some incompatability between g++ (the only C++
compiler available for the paragon) and PVM.  For the record, the
stock master/slave example (made ANSI-compliant) compiles and runs
correctly using gdb, but locks-up on the first pvm call when the EXACT
same code is compiled with g++.

From: "Matthew H. Bassett" <bassett@ecn.purdue.edu>

I have not used PVM in the past year or so but have introduced at
least three people in the department to the power of PVM.  My first
experience with PVM was as a summer intern two summers ago when we
used PVM to parallelize a Monte Carlo batch facility simulation using
the in-house SGI's (16 processors) and Sun (2 processors)
workstations.

The people I have introduced PVM to have used it for Monte Carlo
molecular simulations and parallelizing XPS surface analysis.

From my summer experience I found a drawback was the inability for PVM
to realize that some of the SGI's used were multi-processor machines,
requiring me to spawn extra jobs on these machines manually.  Also the
speed variable never seemed to vary from architecture to architecture
or machine to machine.

Hope that this helps in the improvement of PVM.

Matt

From: Sami Saarinen <sbs@csc.fi>

Jack & the Team,

Here comes my answers!

>   Are you currently using PVM?

Yes.

>   What are your application(s)?

I've implemented the most important (what ever they are!)  MPI calls
with PVM, so that our weather forecast code could make use of MPI
calling syntax during the development phase on IBM SP1. This work
was completed in August. Report is available soon and
a draft is available under http://www.csc.fi/faces/sami.html

I'm being completed with my Parallel Computing guide (written in Finnish)
which practically is fully based on PVM examples. 
(I will send you and Vaidy a copy when its ready; probably in March).

>   How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?

A typically 4-8 machines / nodes from our 24-proc SP2 is allocated to
parallel jobs. They use PVMe 3.x.  But have individuals who run on
other platforms here too. Those systems are: 10 and 6 proc SGI Power
Challenge (R8000) with 2GB and 1GB of memory respectively; SGI-network
of couple of WSs; Convex C3840; Cray XMP-EA/464 (soon to be replaced
by Cray C94). Next year we will start to practice with ~200 node T3E,
too!

>   Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.

The product is great. It's hard to find any weak points except
performance. But I feel that PVM on RISC-stations is a tool for
"proof-of-concept" and a "development platform" for fast
PVM implementations on the proprietary machines/networks like T3E.
Once your idea works on RISC-machines, you can safely transfer it
to faster systems with better performance.

But nevertheless, my wish list contains:

- Please have an option for combination of PvmDataInPlace + PvmDataRaw
- remove stride=1 limitation in PvmDataInPlace messages
- merge pvmd & pvm-group daemons since vendors seem to have done that, too.
  (f.e. on Cray T3D & Convex SPP)

Good luck!

rgds,

Sami

From: merazzi@imacsg1.epfl.ch (S. Merazzi)

Sir, Madam,

This in reply to your request concerning the use of PVM at our group:

Are you using PVM today?
------------------------
Yes, we do.


What are your application(s)?
-----------------------------

Computer simulations by means of finite element/finite volume methods
on parallel computers (T3D/SP2/Paragon/Cenju3).


How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
----------------------------------------------------------

We use PVM in two ways:

1) To distribute data in a Master-Slave environment. The master program
   runs on a front end to a parallel computer. The slaves are
   distributed on the processors of the parallel computer (SPMD
   programming model).  We do not run this programming model in a
   heterogeneous network, i.e. it runs exclusively on T3D/SP2/Paragon.

2) As a communication instrument for a distributed data manager
   (Client-Server concept). 

Thus, we use mostly CRAY-YMP's, Silicon Graphics and SUN's as server
platforms. The parallel computers are T3D, SP2 and Paragon.


Improvements
------------

One can of course always imagine all kinds of improvements. In what
follows I start from the idea that the functionality of PVM is not
modified. Improvements then mostly relate to speed:

1) We notice slow data transfer rates and high start-up (spawn) times
   on the CRAY-YMP/T3D environment. Remedy: ?

2) The XDR data conversion is very slow, especially when working with
   vector computers. Remedy: We have our own optimized tools and we
   run PVM in RAW mode with byte vectors.

3) Communication via daemons is slow (but very convenient!). I
   unfortunately do not know enough of operating systems to imagine how
   it could be improved while maintaining the concept.

I personally do not like the way the daemon has to be started and
managed (and killed here and there). I would appreciate if the PVM
daemon could somehow better be integrated in the operating system.


I am very much impressed by the quality of this public domain
program and the way it is distributed and installed. Thank you and the
PVM team!


I hope that these informations are of some use to you and I remain

Yours sincerely,

Silvio Merazzi
Ecole polyechnique federale de Lausanne
Departement de genie civil
CH-1015 Lausanne
Suisse

tel:   041 21 6932455
mail:  merazzi@pascal.epfl.ch

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
From: Bruno.AGNERAY@ifp.fr (Bruno Agneray)

Q.1 Are you currently using PVM ?
A.1 Yes.

Q.2 What are your application(s) ?
A.2 I am now working on the parallelization of a reflection tomography (or
    travel time inversion). It is a classical technique to obtain velocity and
    reflector information from seismic sections. The great advantage of
    raytracing, when compared for example with finite difference algorithms, is
    that it requests less computing time and memory. Furthermore, the
    parallelization of raytracing is relativly easy since a lot of computations
    can be executed separetly (one computation for one source and one
    reflector).

    The particulars points of this application are :
      * efficient even on loaded network (low unix priority)
      * low impact on interactive work during working hours (low unix priority)
      * dynamically configurable (able to handle addition or deletion of hosts
        during computation (use of pvm_notify and other configuration fonction)
      * fault tolerant (use of pvm_notify and other configuration fonction)
      * strategy of load balancing to overcome that an unique task on a crowded
        machine might remain during hours.

Q.3 How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM ?
A.3 Heterogeneous network of workstations :
      4 SUN SOLARIS
      1 SUN 2 processors SOLARIS.
      2 SGI OS 5.2
      1 SGI 2 processors OS 5.2.
      1 SGI OS 6.0

    Soon :
      RS/6000
      loosely coupled MPP (IBM SP2)


Comments :
  - pvm_notify must be apply to all task (created or to be created).
    It will be interresting to have one pvm_notify for global parallel virtual
    machine or a new flag in pvm_spawn to explicitly ask the notification.
  - In the User's Guide and Tutorial for Networked Parallel Computing, the
    use of struct pvmhostinfo array is not complete at allocation level in that
    way that it is not says if we can desallocate it. 

Best wishes,
