From: "Randy Gressang" <Randy_Gressang@ccmail.sb.grci.com>


     PVM Survey Feedback
     
     1.Are you using PVM today? Currently not using PVM. Have two networks 
     which are candidates for PVM. However, one of the networks has very 
     few UNIX machines on it, and they function as servers. Most machines 
     on the network are 486 class PCs operating under DOS; PVM didn't seem 
     like a good fit. Second network consists of UNIX machines, however it 
     is heavily loaded with applications jobs, and have been unable to 
     convince the organization owning that network that using PVM and 
     converting some of their spaghetti code applications to parallel 
     versions runing under PVM will rationalize network use and free it up.
     
     2.What are your application(s)? The principal application is SAR and 
     ISAR radar image processing and associated automatic target 
     recognition algorithms. Other applications involve neural net "mining" 
     of large distributed data bases.
     
     3.How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM? To date 
     the only machine used has been a single Sun workstation; the problem 
     with using PVM is that it operates under UNIX and most networked 
     computers at this company are PCs operating under DOS, so PVM's full 
     potential cannot be exploited. To exploit PVM's full potential in this 
     commercial environment would require a DOS based version running on a 
     PC. Price and performance of a DOS based PC is such that this 
     commercial LANs is populated with those type machines, and they meet 
     the bulk of requirements. Adding a software capability like PVM to the 
     LAN can be sold to management; replacing most of the machines with 
     UNIX workstations to achieve the PVM capability is perceived by 
     management as too expensive for an ill-defined benefit.

From: Ed Williams <ewilliam@afit.af.mil>
> 
> Are you using PVM today?
Yes.

> 
> What are your application(s)?
Artificial Intelligence -- we are building an inference engine utilizing 
multiple algorithms cooperatively, connected with PVM.

> 
> How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
We have access to around 30 or 40 Sparc20s and 10 Sparc2s; our 
application currently only requires up to 10 systems at a time.

> 
> Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.
An option in the choice of which machines to spawn processes would be 
nice -- currently it is either pick your own or just step through the 
list; it would be nice to be able to let the processes be spawned based 
on the actual processor load, based on the type of machine (given an 
indicator of the magnitude of the task), etc.  Currently I have 
implemented a kludge to do the load-based assignment in my app, but it 
would be nice to have it in PVM.

I have also had problems with the PVM daemon overrunning its buffer in 
situations when I was passing large amounts of data -- I switch to 
routeDirect to solve the problem, but the daemon shouldn't die like that 
-- either it should just stop receiving (back up the sender), let them 
fall on the floor (let the error/resend code handle them) or dynamically 
expand its buffer to handle the load.  My app was sending on the order of 
200,000 34-byte packets in the space of a few minutes -- the slave daemon 
(on the machine with the app that was generating the packets) was the one 
that died.  Once I switched to RouteDirect, the sending app maintains a 
constant 32k send buffer, and the receiving app continuously has a 29-30k 
receive buffer!

> Please email the information to pvm-survey@cs.utk.edu.
> 
> Your help is much appreciated.
Thanks for the great system!


-.-. --.- -.-. --.- -.. . -. -.... --.. --. -. -.... --.. --. .-.-. -.-
Ed Williams (N6ZG)      | PhD Student, Artificial Intelligence
ewilliam@afit.af.mil    | (but if I find the REAL thing, I'll take it too!)

From: deluca@aer.com (Cecelia DeLuca)

Sorry, I hardly ever check this account.  Hope this
is still useful.

Are you using PVM today? No.

What are your application(s)?  I used PVM v3.3 to parallelize
a 2-D atmospheric chemistry model last summer.  The company
I was working for was trying to figure out whether to use
PVM or Linda.  In the full implementation, PVM was a little
faster but they liked Linda better because it was easier to code.

How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
We were running on a Sun MP and around 8 Sun 4's.

Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.
The single biggest hassle with PVM was not being able to send 
and receive common blocks in Fortran.  It would be nice for the
speed-rates in the hosts file to work, too.  Otherwise, I liked 
PVM because commands were very explicit, it was more flexible and
had fewer cute metaphors than Linda, and the documentation 
was outstanding.

From: nico@mikonos.caspur.it (NICO SANNA)
> 
> Are you using PVM today?
  YES.
> 
> What are your application(s)?
  Mainly scientific applications but some industrial codes are going to be ported 
  in paralle using PVM. We have several code running using PVM in the areas of
  Computational chemistry, Fluidodynamics, Mathematics and Engineering.
  We are strongly interested in using PVM to develop and port future scientific
  codes in parallel.
> 
> How many and what kind of machines have you used with PVM?
  About 25 machines including 8 nodes SP2, RS6Ks, ALPHAs & SUNs.
  (More details are available if needed...).
> 
> Any comments and suggestions for improvement are welcome.
  We observe a strong request from the users to put their PVM codes (or vendor
  PVM codes) in PRODUCTION, that is, to have a queuing system capable of manage
  parallel jobs in a heterogeneous (both SW and HW) environment.
  While several queuing systems support PVM jobs, in my opinion, none of them
  fully integrate its capabilities and the management of parallel and serial
  jobs in a multiarchitecture computing system seems to be still a matter of
  study or knoledge of a specific site with specific application.
  May be an improvement of the PVM tool toward the parallel jobs management
  to give a fault-tollerant solution with one or more queueing system, could
  increase its acceptance as 'de-facto standard' message passing tool.

From: Thomas Bahls <bahls@rz.uni-greifswald.de>

Hello all PVM maintainers out there.
 
This is some kind of (positive) feedback. I guess you are interested in ?

I use PVM regularly since version 2.4. So I don't want to express my best
impressions on the software itself. There's no doubt about that.
What's more, I am enthusiastic about the documents available. The PVM User's
Guide was a very useful and beneficial paper in my daily work by now. But a
few weeks ago I was told of the new PVM Book available on netlib. 
I skimmed through it at Easter. 
In my eyes, it's a great guide not only for new PVM users but also for
people who want to get familiar with parallelism. The PVM Book is a good
idea to get a first impression of programming schemes, pitfalls and things
to care of. The author's style, in particular, is really excellent. Compared
with other literature especially in German, the PVM Book is very easy to
understand and offers a quick benefit for practical problems. Its structure
and logic offers a fast access if special information is required.

I don't know who is the extremely talented one writing PVM guides and
manuals. But I want to thank her or him at this point. Because I know lots
of books which are so complicated to use (style, structure, language), I
want you to go on publishing such good work.


Best regards, 
Thomas.
